Christopher D.

2 photos2 check-ins
Bottega Louie is an all time favorite of my family. I have been to both locations, but the downtown LA location holds some special memories. Its high ceilings, beautiful white walls, and fresh flour decorations are luxurious and old world gorgeous. Even the cacophony of voices that echo off the large ceilings add to the luxurious, Italian glow.

My wife and I recently went here for Valentine's Day. I accidentally made a reservation at the other location, but this location was kind enough to accommodate me, which speaks to the service. I will not sometimes the actual food service can be quite slow, but that is inconsistent so I will not damn the restaurant overall for it. However they should improve.

The drinks are awesome. Punchy and alcohol forward. My wife loved the spicy margarita equivalent (forgot the name) from our latest visit. Additionally, there is a healthy wine selection--both local and international.

The food is delicious, rustic, upscale Italian fare. My wife and I have so many favorites: the chicken Parmesan, the portobello mushroom fries, the pappardelle, the bolognese, and of course the tartufo pizza. In addition, the bakery has an amazing selection of desserts, with my wife and I loving the beignets and the macarons.

Prices are high-ish, but not offensively so. Think 30-50 per plate and maybe $75pp with a drink. So not at all terrible. All in, I highly recommend Bottega and think everybody should try it.

Ambiance: 5/5
Service: 4/5
Drinks: 4.5/5
Food: 5/5
Price: 4/5
Consistency: 4/5

Portobello Fries

Chicken Parmesan

After attending an amazing evening concert at the Crypto Arena...

Followed by a night full of shaking what my momma gave me at a local Latin club in DTLA...

Then finally hitting the pillow in the early hours of the morning and sleeping like an absolute baby at the coolest Downtown Boutique Hotel...

YOU KNOW for a fact that as much as my wife & I missed our three kids who we'd left overnight with their Auntie...

We were just not quite ready to return to reality.

So on the way home the next morning before making our way to the 101 fwy...

We decided Sunday Brunch was in order and what better place to brunch it up then....

BOTTEGA LOUIE in Downtown Los Angeles!!!!

Wait? What??

You've never heard of Bottega Louie??

Well, you my friend....

Are. In. For. A. Treat.

Hey, if anyone knows how to Brunch...

It's. The. French.

And I don't know about you...

But I'm pretty sure the French Revolution was really started over Brunch and not over Social & Political upheaval like the history books claim ;)

So yeah, for those of you whom haven't been to B.L. Yet, let me tell ya....

From the moment you walk in, you are instantly transformed into another world.

From the World Class Baked Goods....

Just wait until you see all of the goodies behind their glass case lines.

(From their Beignets and Croissants to their Fruit Tarts and colorful Macarons) if you have a sweet tooth...

You. Will. Definitely. Be. In. Trouble.

And that's JUST THE BEGINNING!!

If you happen to make it past all the baked goods, and stay for Sunday Brunch, be prepared to have your mind FREAKIN' blown!

My wife went with their Le Pancake (a Soufflé-Style Pancake with Chantilly Cream & Strawberry Sauce)

-----Sounds Fancy doesn't it-----

and her eyes nearly rolled into the back of her head, I thought she was gonna have a...

oh never mind =)

As for me...

Mine was good, but apparently not that good ;)

I had their Croque Madame Sandwich (Jambon de Paris, Melted Gruyère, Dijon & Béchamel with a sunny side egg on sliced pain de mie) accompanied by THE cutest arugula salad ever...

Let's just say....

I was ready to meet my maker that day!

Yeah, it was that dang GOOD!

We did share their $10 glass of Fresh Squeezed O.J. (TOTALLY WORTH IT) by the way...

(We were in awe about the family next to us who had about $50 bucks worth of O.J. at their table)...

Ballers!!! LOL

And of course we each had a beautiful Cappuccino to start our morning off RIGHT!

Other Brunch Specialties that caught my eye and are definitely on my radar for our next Brunch outing here are....

-The Lobster Hash ($35)

-The 16oz bone in Ribeye with Eggs ($65!!!)

-The Tartufo Pizza (Mozzarella, Fontina, truffle pecorino, crème fraîche, black truffle mushroom pâté, soft cooked egg & shaved Sabatino black truffles) ($50)

So, who's coming with me and which one are you getting??

I know you ladies are all getting the 'Le Pancake'

LOL

Of course Lunch & Dinner are also Top of The Class
and you really can't go wrong with anything this place has.

This DTLA location is their original spot, but they also have a location which we've stopped by once before for some Macarons to go in WEHO (West Hollywood) which BTW has THE FANCIEST restroom that I have EVER seen in my ENTIRE LIFE!!

So if you find yourself in Los Angeles...

Visiting, on business, or just for pleasure....

Do yourself a solid and come to Bottega Louie and

GET one of EVERYTHING!!!

The Louie salad is a namesake of the place. The salad was a relic from the past. Very 80's with thousand island dressing, but modernized with the cut up lettuce. We added an extra chicken breast to boost the protein. The burrata pizza was delicious. The crust is light and airy with the right amount of crunch.

A must order is the chocolate soufflé. It was light and just sweet enough to curb that sugar fix. One of the best desserts that I've had in a while.

The place is huge, but feels stark with the white walls. They call it minimalist, I guess. Service was excellent. My suggestion would be to make a reservation so you don't need to wait. He was attentive and gave great advice on the food. Super knowledgeable and smart.

The pastries look delicious, almost too good to eat. Perhaps next time when I'm not stuffed, I'll grab one.

It isn't cheap with almost $100 for the entire meal, but the quality is in the details!

Whether you're here for a meal, a drink at the cafe bar area, or to check out the beautiful pastries section. This place will leave your mouth watering. I've been quite a few times as well as the West Hollywood location. Both great and completely different from each other. Downtown location has that open high ceiling New York vibe. A beautiful pastries section right when you walk in with all the artful creation in the glass display. Plus the famous macarons all lined up.

West Hollywood, a smaller location but it does have patio seating in front as well as covered patio out back. More lush garden vibe. And their pastries and bar area is right in the middle of the restaurant. Both beautifully decorated which gives it that extra touch. Didn't have a meal this time but desserts were picked up at the downtown location for a special night. My bday of course...Lol... If you haven't had any of their pastries, it's a must. Each items are well decorated and beautifully made that you don't want to eat them. And their famous macarons, bite size goodies. They are a little on the pricey side but worth it. Cakes are amazing which is great for gathering or a hostess gift. We had the fruit tart which is somewhat seasonal as during the summer it wasn't available the last time. It was replaced with a peach tart. Still amazing though. I assume as it was a seasonal fruit, it was brought out for the summer.

Fruit tart is alway a top choice for us as it's pretty simple but oh so good. A nice crunchy base but flakey. Filled with a delicious custard and topped with amazing berries. A slice is great but a whole cake is better. Regardless whatever you choose, there's never a wrong thing. Only thing that sucks, they can't write anything for you. If it's a birthday, they'll add a chocolate bday sign instead.

Parking is a stretch at this location. Valet or a parking structure. Street parking is a bitch downtown. But you can't go wrong with Bottega....

Gina M.
Upland, CA
8 Italian Food reviews
Feb 6, 2026
3 photos1 check-in
I went to an early dinner at Bottega Louie in Downtown Los Angeles, and it was my first time visiting with a friend, so I really didn't know what to expect.

They offer a variety of menu options -- sandwiches, pastas, pizzas, and salads -- but since they're known for their pizza, we decided to split one.

We ordered the Margherita pizza and asked if we could add a few vegetables. We originally wanted bell peppers, but they didn't have those available as an add-on. Instead, we added olives and a vegetable topping that was similar to broccoli.

The crust was thin, which some people may really like. My friend enjoyed it more than I did -- for me, it was just okay. I think I was expecting a little more flavor or richness. It almost tasted a bit "too healthy" for what I usually want from a pizza -- LOL. I did have a few slices, but if I go back, I'd probably try a different style of pizza.

One thing that did surprise us was the bill -- they added $5 for the veggie add-ons plus a surcharge. We were a little shocked by that, but when we asked about it, they did remove the charge, which we appreciated.

Overall, the restaurant itself is beautiful. The space is elegant, open, and very aesthetically pleasing. Even the bathrooms were stunning -- decorated in gold and white and very pretty.

Our waitress was very nice and attentive, which made the experience even better.

They also have a front dessert counter filled with beautiful pastries and desserts that looked amazing. I didn't try any this time, but I would definitely love to come back and sample a few on my next visit.

I would definitely go back again -- but next time, I'd try a different pizza or maybe explore some of their other menu items (and dessert!).

Such a beautiful, luxe restuarant with great food and pretty pastries. I loved the bright and elegant decor/atmosphere - it made the experience really enjoyable. The open kitchen was fun, too. We got the sausage pizza and it was some of the best pizza we've ever had - thin with an ultra-crispy crust and the perfect ratio of sauce, cheese, and toppings. My cobb salad was really good, too! The complimentary bread was cute and fresh/warm - tasted a bit floury but it was good with the butter.

I liked their macarons, though pistachio tasted a tad artificial and earl grey was slightly too bitter. The plain croissant and pain au chocolat were just ok. The pain au chocolat barely had chocolate in it. The chocolate eclair (with a chocolate cream filling) was good, but on the drier/denser side.

The atmosphere and dine-in food were the stars. The patries were gorgeous but nothing special taste-wise. Overall, I highly recommend - this was worth the trip!

Bottega Louie is a restaurant, gourmet market, patisserie and cafe, with full bar service. This place looks beautiful on the inside. There are two seating areas: one where you wait to be seated in the restaurant and another where you can seat yourself next to the pastry displays. There is also an open kitchen, which I really like.

Brunch: The eggs benedict was good, but nothing to be amazed at. I preferred the spinach and goat cheese omelette. The egg of the omelette was very light and fluffy. It was generously packed with baby spinach, onions, bell papers, and goat cheese. My favorite thing though was the portobello fries. These are a must! They were so crispy on the outside and juicy on the inside. It comes with a delicous aioli sauce.

Pastries: Tried the blueberry goat cheese macaron and I was impressed. I didn't expect to like this flavor as much as I did. I see why there macarons are so popular now. Definitely their best pastry. I enjoyed the chocolate eclair as well, but wouldn't pay $8 for it again. Least favorite pastry was the beignet. It was mediocre at best.

Closest parking lot is across the street. It is cheaper than valet parking.

Bottega Louie - DTLA

Bottega Louie never misses. From the moment you walk in, the ambiance is unreal - bright, lively, and framed by those gorgeous high ceilings that make the whole space feel grand. The open kitchen adds to the vibe, letting you watch the action while you wait (and drool a little).

The pastries are absolutely elite (the macarons are dangerous), the brunch menu is always on point, and the staff is consistently great and friendly, even when the place is slammed.

It's one of those spots where you can take anyone - friends, coworkers, out-of-towners -- and everyone leaves impressed. Beautiful space, great food, and top-tier vibes. A DTLA staple for a reason.

It IS very loud due to the wall-to-wall marble, so that's really my only negative, but it's not overwhelming.

Bottega Louie is undeniably beautiful -- bright, airy, aesthetic, and just a really fun place to walk into. It has that iconic LA vibe that makes it perfect for bringing out-of-town visitors who want something memorable and visually stunning. I had a friend visiting from out of the country and staying nearby, so I wanted to take her somewhere special for brunch. I'd heard a lot about Bottega Louie and was excited to try it for the first time. We went on a Sunday morning during brunch and I made reservations expecting it to be packed, but it actually wasn't too busy. There were people, but it wasn't overwhelming at all. Parking is mostly street parking, so definitely give yourself some extra time to find a spot. They also have valet parking available, which is convenient if you don't want to circle the blocks. The service at the front was just okay -- not rude, but not particularly welcoming either. Once seated, the service was fine but nothing memorable. For brunch, we ordered the waffles, avocado toast, a burger, salmon benedict and a matcha latte. Honestly, everything was just okay. Nothing was bad, but nothing really stood out flavor-wise. I was honestly a bit underwhelmed. We didn't try the desserts this time since we had plans to go somewhere else afterward, but the dessert counter looked gorgeous. Overall, the ambience and aesthetic definitely outshine the food and service. I'm glad I tried it once, especially to take my visiting friend somewhere pretty and iconic, but it's probably not a place I'd return to.

Aug 31, 2025Previous review
Always a pleasure, and never a disappointment after coming here for 12 years. A fabulous French patisserie and bakery, amazing macarons, a woodfired on site, pizza and bread, oven, and need to order Italian pastas, pizzas, salads, and equally great entrées make for a great experience for everyone from small singles and couples to larger parties. Created in the original women's wear department of one of Los Angeles's oldest and most luxurious department stores, this place stands the test of time from maintaining the highest quality and some of the best service available in downtown Los Angeles. Non-validated parking is available across the street on Grand Avenue between 7th and 8th Street. But it's also an easy one block stroll from the 7th and Metro West exit. They do take both Reservations and have a waitlist for tables. The restaurant is also ADA accessible. There are a number of V/V+ selections as well. Also, there's a full bar in the front that features happy hours directly across from the patisserie and bakery. Because this is a large department store space, ambience can be quite noisy and echoes because of all of the white marble surfaces, probably not the best place for intimate and quiet conversations.

Mar 14, 2015Previous review
After skating a Pershing Square, we noticed this while walking the revised downtown lofty-artsy-theatry-dog salony-still a few homelessy district.

Since an oddly large number of my friends have also eaten here, and I was just passing through the first-time to check out the bakery, time to eat.

Simple formula - avoid everything Carlyn ate, order things Clara, Megumi and Edwin liked, then improvise per the advice of their unbelievely well-trained staff.

Made the $20 pizza my own: 1/2 artichoke and 1/2 burrata - it's like having Batalli's burrata bar on a perfect 1000F fired crust. There: appropriate value for the price, accomplished (it's about a 16-inch medium-large)

Hit the mezze plates: Grilled octopus - perfect. sauteed kale sprouts - nice. duck prosciutto crostini - can I have a hoagie-sized version of this?

Trenne - triangular penne with a crisp-edge from the pan-fry afterwards with a rib eye-based red sauce that rocks (I'd double the sauce, just because)

Desserts - the peanut butter terrine figured out how to make peanut butter fluffy and wedge it into a napoleon - nice and not overly sweet. Butterscotch budino - went even better with almond gelato added. Ditto with those beignets (which, depending on your comparison with New Orleans, may not strictly really be beignets and more like round raised donuts...) which were great with some more gelato to go with the raspberry puree. Btw, croissants are great here.

The place used to be a designer fashion salon, so the high-ceilings do make it sort of like eating inside a cathedral, din-wise.

As to the difficulty with seating, because the place is so huge and the staff so efficient, we waited all of exactly 16.5 minutes at the peak of a Saturday night dinner hour at 7 pm for a table for 2. Bigger parties, definitely have to plan, because they don't accept reservations. However there is a open bar area to bide your wait-times, and there's always the bakery.

And don't forget to say, "Hi." to the blue-feathered fellow in the cafe area.

Louie Salad ($25)

Hamburger ($25)
Medium well done burger was perfect and still very juicy. It's a nice thick patty. The bun got soggy already though. Huge portion and LOTS of fries. They were nice and crispy but not too stiff. Comes with three sauces (ketchup, some kind of spicy mayo?, and mustard) and pickles.

Pistachio Gelato ($12)
HUGE scoop and no artificial colors! The flavor is perfect and not too sweet. Comes with a crunchy sweet thing which I didn't like because it's too hard and sticks to my teeth. Doesn't break down easily.

Yuzu Calamansi Eclair ($8)
I personally don't really like eclairs because they're a bit hard and dry. But I love the strong yuzu flavor of this. Nice and citrusy.

It's pricey but a nice treat once in a while.

The server was very friendly.

I love this place's brunch!!! We came here on the 4th of July and had no wait whatsoever. Not that we would have minded because the bakery in front is a sugar addict's dream! Tons of cute macarons (wrapped up in fancy boxes a la Laduree), elaborate pastries and plenty of space.

The Lemon Ricotta Pancakes with blueberry syrup was scrumptious. My friends enjoyed both the Lobster Hash and BLT, but didn't like the BLT bread (completely toasted, so messy to eat).

They have tons of gluten-free options on the menu, so they won major bonus points from our celiac friend for that! Plus, our server was so friendly and knowledgeable about the menu. I'm coming back here for brunch every time I'm in LA!

Bakery: Their most popular macaron ($2.50 + tax) is the Salted Caramel, but I went for the Earl Grey (delicious and chocolate-y creme filling) and Pistachio (meh).

The only possible cons I could think of are the metered parking and lack of decor. It's such a huge, airy space that the blank walls and plain structural beams are begging for adornment - even just crown moulding and a few wall sconces would help. But those are the only negatives!

I went in to visit for the first time get grab a little dessert treat with my husband and kids. The cashier was very pleasant and praised my choice in dessert choices.

The four of us shared a piece of decadent chocolate cake called Le Noir and a we shared a mini fruit tart. The chocolate cake slice was chocolatey heaven. The flavors are soft yet rich at the same time. It is not overly sweet.

The fruit tart was the star, however. The natural sweetness of the raspberries and blueberries were really brought forward by the soft and heavenly creamy custard filling of the tart. Underneath the creamy custard, there is a thin layer smashed blueberries - almost like a preserve, but it tastes very fresh and amazingly delicious.

I do wish there was another location that has more accessible parking. Downtown LA parking is never something that is easy to come by, but the desserts here are worth it.

A timeless Los Angeles institution still setting the standard for excellence.

Andre Miripolsky and I had dinner last night at Bottega Louie in downtown Los Angeles, and it reminded me why this restaurant remains one of the cornerstones of LA's culinary identity. From the moment we arrived, the service was exceptional. I started with a perfectly balanced dirty martini at the bar -- cold, crisp, and beautifully prepared.

Andre ordered the chef salad and immediately said it was the best he's ever had. I had the braised beef, which ranks among the best dishes I've had anywhere, period. Every detail, from the preparation to the presentation, reflected the same precision and consistency that made Bottega Louie a downtown landmark years ago.

Having grown up around fine dining and spent years working in Michelin-level environments before graduate school and law, I can say without hesitation that what they've achieved here deserves recognition. This place has helped define downtown Los Angeles as an international destination, and it continues to perform at the highest level.

Thank you Ivan, you did a wonderful job.

Highly recommended.

Viva LA and Fear No Art

Andre and I present two masterpieces from Bottega Louie -- the chef salad and braised beef, both absolute perfection.

Bottega Louie located at grand and 7th St. Downtown Los Angeles.

Aimes O.
Elite 26
Los Angeles, CA
54 Brunch reviews
Mar 28, 2025
4 photos
We hosted our friend's baby shower at Bottega Louie and it was absolutely perfect. The restaurant is already stunning on its own--with its airy white interiors, beautiful marble accents, and elegant ambiance--but once we added our table décor, it looked like something out of a magazine. So many other guests in the restaurant were stopping to take pictures of our setup, which says a lot!

We went with Menu IV ($55 per guest) served family style, and honestly, it was worth every penny. The viennoiserie assortment of pastries and croissants was buttery and flaky, and the avocado toast with basil aioli and poached egg was a crowd favorite. Every single item on the menu was delicious, from the decadent French toast with raspberry compote and sliced almonds, to the perfectly seasoned breakfast potatoes, to the creamy Greek yogurt topped with fresh berries and candied walnuts.

The scrambled eggs were not as light and fluffy as I typically would like, but they remade them for me! The bacon was thick-cut and crispy (a must!), and the smoked salmon platter with bagels and cream cheese was so fresh and satisfying. And just when we thought we couldn't eat any more--dessert came out. The macarons were as tasty as they were beautiful, and the beignets with raspberry sugar and compote were melt-in-your-mouth good.

The service was attentive and friendly throughout, and the staff made sure everything flowed smoothly. Bottega Louie made our special event even more memorable, and we couldn't recommend it more for brunches, showers, or any celebration. We'll definitely be back!

What We Ordered:

-Pistachio Latte Iced 16 OZ $6.50
-Macaron of the Month: Butterscotch Brandy $3

Pre-Valentine's Day Celebration with the Wife. We had a lunch plans at Tokyo Fried Chicken and had time to kill and stopped by Bottega Louie to see what kind speciality items they have for Valentine's Day.

We ordered via the app as this is the only method to receive rewards at Bottega, unfortunately.

We always try the speciality of the month and we opted to do the same today. The Butterscotch Brandy (contains alcohol) was very good and a nice treat to share with the wife.

The Pistachio Latte was okay, but the flavor wasn't evenly distributed as we didn't taste pistachio syrup until the end, which was a bit of a bummer.

This is a great place to sit and chat and people watch all the interesting folks walking by.

The tables need to be bussed faster. A lot of tables were dirty with crumbs and they are bit slow to properly clean the tables.

My oblivious wife put her arm against the table and when she lifted it up. There were crumbs all over her sleeve. Y'all gotta get together!

We'll be back again soon to see what specials they have for Easter!

Pro Tip: Don't be discouraged if you don't see the pastry you want available on the app. It's better to go there and see for yourself. Many times management is too busy to reload the pastries on the app. I frequently go to order on the app and several items show out of stock. but I see it in front of me inside the case. You can order it on kiosk or at the register, but you won't get rewards points as it shows not available on the app. Which is annoying, but it is what is.

Dec 31, 2024Previous review
What We Ordered:

-Gingerbread Latte Iced
-Eggnog Latte
-Eggnog Macaroon
-Creme Brûlée Donut
-Raspberry Chocolate

I came here alone, and my wife was super jealous and complained that I never took her to good spots. Whoops! My boss (wife) had a wife coming up; I decided it was time to prove her wrong.

They have an app where you can order things and accumulate reward points. However, sometimes, they are slow to put the items in stock on the app. I went there around 9 am on a weekday, and items were showing sold out in the app, but they had them in stock. I was told that the manager had yet to load them into the system. Be aware! Some items claiming to be sold out on the app may be available when you come in person. They need to get better at that. When you order in person, you are unable to claim reward points, which is another annoying aspect.

The Eggnog Macaroon was great but it has alcohol in it. Be aware!

They were sold out of the eggnog latte, and instead of giving me a refund to my card like they said. A credit was issued to my account on the app, which is a bit annoying because I was told differently.

The Gingerbread Latte was pretty good! I wish we could have tried the Eggnog latte, but all good.

The Creme Brûlée Donut was excellent. I love the croissant-like texture and rich filling inside. It was a real treat!

The wife opted for the Raspberry Chocolate Cake, and she liked it so much. It was pretty good - I'm not going to lie.

I really like Bottega Louie, but why have an app if you can't use it properly? They need to figure that out and have better systems in place.

I would easily give them five stars for food and drink, but knocking two stars off for not being able to use the rewards on the app and not getting the credit back to my credit card for a sold-out drink like I was told.

What I Order:

-16 oz Pumpkin Pie Latte $6.50
-Napoleon $16
-Box of 13 Macaroons $40

This is the most-reviewed business on Yelp, with over 19,000 reviews! The benefit of living in a foodie city like LA is being able to visit so many amazing places. I had Bottega Louie bookmarked on my list for a while now. I finally decided it was time to give this place a try. I ordered a season latte called the Pumpkin Pie Latte, which I was told was very popular. It was pretty good. It wasn't as good as Starbucks' Pumpkin Spiced Latte, but it was much better than the others I tried.

I was also told that Napoleon was popular and worth a try. I thought it was pretty good. The filling was very decadent and sweet, which I loved, but there were too many flaky layers, which I didn't eat as it was too much. Eating with the plastic utensils they gave you was also very difficult. It would be easier to eat with proper silverware. I want to try other pastries and cakes next time. I don't think the Napoleon was worth the price.

The smallest-sized box of macaroons is 13 pieces. You can place a smaller order, but it will come inside a bag, not one of those pretty little pink boxes with bows. I opted to get two boxes of 13 macaroons as they were a gift for some people. I heard the macaroons were incredible. My friend said they were better than those she had in Paris. That speaks volumes to the quality of macaroons at Bottega Louie.

I will be back to try some delicious cakes, and I hope to try another seasonal latte.

We were just refused service in the cafe for the second time. I have been a customer since opening day at this 7th street staple of downtown LA. I am sad to report that service has taken a back seat to something ? at this revered foodie Mecca. Don't misunderstand my point, the food is impeccable, atmosphere dynamic, fresh and lively......but, and this is a big BUT! don't come here in the morning and expect the staff to serve you and your colleagues coffee or a croissant if you casually take a seat in the cafe.

After a decade of a service and customer focused approach to hospitality, I am sad to report: Bottega Louie has change their attitude. Apparently new Managment has directed staff to dismiss you to "get your own coffee at the front counter". Frankly Mr. Louie, this is an insult! What happened to this place? I can't recommend it for a drop in meeting nor a quick break. It's always a good choice for lunch or dinner, but this previously top rated spot has fallen far down the recommended list. Thank goodness there are plenty of options close by.

I've been dining at Bottega Louie for 13 years, and somehow it never disappoints. Every visit still feels like a first love.

The desserts are as stunning as ever--tiny works of art that taste as good as they look. The pasta with jumbo shrimp was delicious (originally it's with lobster, but our waiter kindly swapped it since they were out that day), and heirloom burrata salad were perfect. Even the simple Epi bread with butter, served right on the paper-lined table, feels effortlessly chic.

Funny thing: for some reason, I always end up here with old friends I haven't seen in years--and every single time, we take a photo in front of the dessert display. Same spot, same smiles, different year. Maybe it's fate... or just really good lighting.

After all these years, Bottega Louie still feels like the heart of downtown--beautiful, delicious, and timeless.

Jun 6, 2025
I've always seen so many fancy pictures of Bottega Louie, seen it gifted to people, and also have had it suggested to me whenever I'm within the LA vicinity, so I was pretty excited to finally try their desserts after so long.

We came during Valentine's Day, so it was quite packed, both the restaurant side and the side ordering from the to go bakery section. However, there was a kiosk without anyone there, so we ordered from there for pick up quite quickly.

I got the:
1) Beignet:
-I love beignets, so when I saw that they had one, I knew I had to try it.
-Maybe I've been spoiled by the Beignets Expressed or even Disney, but this just tasted like a standard sugar donut to me. Nothing to write home about. (Judge me if you will for my troglodyte tastes)

2) Macarons:
-I got the Grand Cru, Early Grey, and Salted Caramel flavors.
-They were definitely a feast for the eyes. Especially the Earl Grey one with the blue coloring and dash of gold. Reminds me of a precious bird's egg. The Grand Cru was a lovely bright red, and the Salted Caramel was a deep sienna color. All very delicate with the perfect texture in a bite. Sweet, yummy small treat.
-I just got the Grand Cru since I've never heard of it before, but it tasted like a slightly richer chocolate? Not sure if there's any hint of wine or because the cocoa was sourced somewhere specific, but its decent.
-Salted caramel had a gooey caramel filling, which was decadently perfect and the Earl Grey had a stronger tea taste with slight sweetness which was nice.

Would love to eventually try their restaurant and of course more of their bakery goods.

Bottega Louie is very well known for their pastries and macarons. So I've only ever gotten those. Until a recent invitation for brunch came around. We had reservations for a huge party of 12 on a Sunday. We waited about 15 minutes to be seated.

For starters, we got their Brussels Sprouts, the Modena salad, and a few orders of their Portobello fries with aioli (so so good!). Everyone enjoyed the apps. We ordered a few of their pizzas to share, pepperoni for the kids, the Burrata (with proscuitto) & Tartufo (truffle overload) pizza for the adults. Love the pizza here, thin almost chewy crust and they don't skimp on the toppings. We also ordered some from their brunch menu - the Farmer's Market breakfast was okay. Definitely way too overpriced and under seasoned for just poached eggs over veggies. Lol. The Eggs Benedict and the French Toast are delicious. We enjoyed the espresso martinis and their Italian sodas and ended with a variety of sweets like their eclairs and mini cakes.

Impeccable service. Love their pastries and desserts. Definitely on the pricier end. Loved the vibes and especially the cathedral ceilings. It made the place feel not as crowded as it was. Would stop by again for the pastries if in the area.

Ted H.
Elite 26
Rowland Heights, CA
23 Brunch reviews
Mar 9, 2025
A beautiful indoor spot in DTLA. There is no valet or onsite parking. I usually aim to park at LAZ Parking 725 S Grand Ave, Los Angeles, CA 90017, which is across the street on the northwest side of Bottega Louie.

So now you've parked, braved the parking structure pee smells, and walked across the street. Center yourself. Goodness is on the horizon.

As you enter you are greeted by the bakery/take-out, or turn to the host at the little table. It is helpful to have reservations, especially during peak times. They use resy.com BUT, if they time you'd like is not available online, just call them at 213-802-1470 and ask! You never know, and many a time they take me right away.

I have only ever eaten here for lunch, and it is usually a business meeting. It can be loud at times due to the glass, open air, and no "soft" furniture. But the staff is usually very attentive and doesn't constantly interrupt you, but still takes the time to refill drinks and be available if signaled.

My go to is their Cobb Salad, which is massive and full of bacon, egg, chicken, fresh avocado and all the good stuff you'd expect. Runs around $25

I usually get an arnold palmer, but our guests like the italian sodas...and there is a full bar. Get some baked goods for the ride home on your way out.

Olena A.
Los Angeles, CA
8 Brunch reviews
Feb 3, 2025
10 photos
Bottega Louie transports you to another world where Italian classics meet an elevated French bistro experience. This location in particular is very grand with the high ceilings and minimalist decor. I would recommend just stopping by to admire the beautiful pastries and macaron display.

I was drawn to the Branzino on the menu which is a tender white fish that's grilled with tender meat and crispy skin. The fish was very well done - so buttery and rich, but perfectly balanced with the light and lemony frisée salad of watercrest. This dish did take a while to cook so make sure to order yourself an appetizer while you wait.

With that being said, I ordered the Portobello fries which are thick cut, portobello mushrooms, in a thick Parmesan batter. There are a lot of great reviews on yelp about these but I did not enjoy them like many others did. I found the powder to be too thick for the mushroom which made the "fry" dense. With the mushroom being a very absorbent vegetable, it was very oily on the inside. With the cilantro aïoli, it was a very dense and oily appetizer - a huge contrast to the light and flavorful fish.

I did, however, find the service to be very professional, and the waiter guided me through my decision to land on the Branzino.

I would definitely come back for a pizza or pasta sometime!

Dessert: 4/5
Service: 3.5/5
Ambiance: 5/5
Price: $$$

This review is based on dessert only and not related to the food.

Me and my friends were craving for dessert and saw this place still open at 10pm, so we get on our car and head on to Bottega Louie. Upon arriving, the place was mostly empty since many people already done with their dinner. We got seated at the bar area and ordered a couple dessert with the bartender.

Two out of three desserts we order was absolutely fantastic! The fruit tart was exceptional and refreshing in a way. The pistachio gelato was probably the best I've had. A little note that I'm not a fan of pistachio, yet I had to admit that it was delicious. You can really taste the nuttiness and pistachio chunks and flavor.

The Le Noir was an absolute disappointment! It was hard almost like a brick. We were wondering if we came here too late at night that the cake is already tucked in some freezer. If that's the case, we might never know. But I can tell that the texture was hard when I was expecting soft and bouncy cake.

I'm definitely going back for the food next time and the dessert next time (not the Le Noir of course, i would stay clear of that). Until next time!

Dessert Time! (Le Noir in the front and Fruit Tart in the distance)

Mar 28, 2025
8 photos
Came back to Bottega Louise for our anniversary left a lasting impression. The restaurant offers a fancy yet welcoming atmosphere that immediately sets the tone for the night.

We started with the calamari, which was delish - crisp on the outside, tender on the inside, with just the right amount of seasoning. The crab cake was just as amazing, super tasty.

The main dish was undoubtedly the truffle pizza. The combination of a perfectly crisp crust, rich truffle taste in every bite, and carefully selected toppings created a flavor profile that was nothing short of extraordinary.

To complement our meal, we ordered their sweet dessert wine and a bubbly Italian soda.

Service was amazing - friendly, attentive, and professional. The staff demonstrated an extensive knowledge of the menu and made our anniversary memorable with the candle! I wish I knew the name of our waitress so I could give her a shoutout!!

It's worth noting that valet parking comes at a price of $20, which might seem steep to some. However, the convenience and overall quality of the dining experience more than justify the additional cost.

Highly recommended for date nights, and anyone looking to elevate their dining experience. Try to truffle pizza!!

The prices are pretty expensive compared to other Italian places but you are in downtown LA so you're going to pay prices according to the area. Service was great. Bottega Louie is a staple restaurant in DTLA. It's a beautiful space with marble flooring that make noises reverberate throughout the restaurant. It can make it difficult to hear table conversations. They take reservations for large parties and recommended for the busy brunch or dinner hours. They are across the street from LAZ Parking ($7 flat rate after 4pm) - convenient and much cheaper than valet.

For the food: They have many options to keep everyone in the party satisfied - order family-style to try more options. The bakery may be better than the food. They are famous for the macarons. Here are some of my favorite dishes:

- MODENA Salad
- CALABRESE Pizza
- CACIO E PEPE Pasta
- BRUSSELS SPROUTS & WALNUTS
- BURRATA & HEIRLOOM TOMATOES
- PORTOBELLO FRIES - Must Order
- TUNA TARTARE
- SALMON
- SHORT RIB
- LE NOIR
- FRUIT TART
- Macarons: SALTED CARAMEL, EARL GREY, LEMON - Must Order

The Napoleon cake is the best I've ever had; it's sweet but not cloying, and even those who don't have a big sweet tooth should try it. Bottega Louie has been on my list of LA restaurants to try for a while. Cute ambiance, solid reviews and tasty looking pictures. Let's start with the pros - service and drinks. I was seated quickly on a busy Sunday night without a reservation and my waiter was attentive. The pear martini is soooo good. It's a bit sweet but still very good. Cons - the food. I asked the waiter what they're known for so I got the caesar salad, portobello fries, Margherita pizza, and le noir for dessert. It was a grocery store salad, greasy and heavy portobello fries, flavorless pizza and publix chocolate cake (publix cake is a tad better). Overall, it's a casual restaurant with a high end reputation.

Morgan H.
Elite 26
Long Beach, CA
220 Brunch reviews
Mar 27, 2024
1 photo
We made a last minute reservation for 1:30pm on a Saturday and I was glad we had one because this place was buzzing! It's been around for quite some time now and hasn't waned in popularity. The interior is lavish and bright with tall ceilings. Upon entering you're greeted by their colorful display of fresh macarons and a full patisserie. It's a good idea to pick up a sweet treat after your meal.

At the time of our reservation the brunch menu was being served. The menu seems to be a mix of French and Italian, and they offer traditional brunch options as well. We decided to split the Mache salad which was exquisite. So bright and fresh, it was a mix of flavorful shredded roasted chicken, celery, avocado, julienned snap peas and a lemon vinaigrette with micro viola flowers. Stunning.

We rounded out the meal with the Burrata Pizza. It's topped with mozzarella, super fresh burrata and prosciutto, and a bit of sautéed rapini. You can see them cooking it in the open woodfired pizza oven and they are LARGE. You could split one between 3-4 people depending on what else you order. We absolutely loved it and took home leftovers.

Burrata Pizza

Lissa L.
Elite 26
All-Star
La Verne, CA
12 Brunch reviews
Feb 27, 2024
3 photos
Bottega Louie's all-white interiors are the perfect backdrop for the star of the show - the pastries in the display case and the food. Your eye is drawn to the colors displayed on the wall (they offer boxed chocolates and sprinkles-covered pretzels) to entice you into buying their treats. It's a great way to minimize visual clutter.

The service was top-notch. The servers are knowledgeable about the food and the alcoholic beverages offered. They make it a point to ask about allergies and food sensitivities. This is LA, after all. ;)

My short rib was enjoyable. The tender meat along with some polenta and that savory sauce made for the perfect bite.

Their portobello fries were crispy and not overly battered. It was just crunch after satisfying crunch in my mouth. Paired with their green sauce, it was *chef's kiss* an excellent appetizer.

My hubby had the club sandwich and it was an elevated version of the classic. The potato chips were made in-house and didn't feel greasy. Just thick, hearty and starchy goodness!

One issue I had was the lack of any acoustic control. It was difficult to hear everybody else at the table. I'm not sure why, but it sounded louder in there than it actually was. We were there on a weeknight and given that it was around 8pm, there were few guests. Perhaps a sound engineer could come over and see what could be done. The sounds tended to saturate only in some areas.

Another issue I had was that the server kept forgetting my drink order. It was minor, though I had to follow up with him twice, and another time with the guy who brought us dessert. It was only when I was done with my meal that he remembered to finally bring it, along with a slightly audible apology. It's okay. The food and the ambiance made up for it. Bottega Louie will always live up to your expectations. :o)

Restaurant, bakery, and it's pretty? Sign me up.

A friend recommended Bottega Louie during our short and sweet visit to LA. I asked for coffee and brunch spots and BL checked all the boxes. We didn't have a reservation for the restaurant, and were informed about a long-ish wait when we arrived. However, they said the cafe seating area is first come, first serve and we can still order from the restaurant menu from there. Since we had a long drive back to Phoenix that day and didn't want to wait, we decided to sit in the cafe. It worked out just fine!

We ordered the following:
Smoked salmon benedict $32
Lobster hash $35
Le pancake $26
Latte

The smoked salmon benedict came with poached eggs, smoked salmon, red
onions, sautéed spinach, hollandaise sauce, crème fraîche, and hash brown potato galettes. The lobster hash came with lobster, two poached eggs, potato, leek & scallion hash cakes, tender greens, and lobster beurre monté. The le pancake was a large soufflé pancake served with fresh strawberries, Chantilly cream, and strawberry compote. The presentation was beautiful. My family of three shared everything so we could sample each item. All the entrees tasted fresh and delicious, but my favorite was the lobster hash. The latte was solid, too.

We had to make a stop at the bakery and take some treats before leaving. I chose a box of six macarons, mostly different flavors as well as their version of Suprême's NY roll, the chocolate pistachio flavor. The pastries were pretty and tasty, but none of them blew my mind.

Our server was fantastic. He was pleasant and responsive. Though the food was great, the portions are meant for a light brunch, in my opinion. Overall, we had a lovely experience and think it's worth visiting!

See all photos from Gretel Y. for Bottega Louie

28 Brunch reviews
Apr 14, 2024
8 photos
Lively ambiance with modern and minimalistic interior, Bottega Louie is a combination of an Italian restaurant, gourmet market, and French patisserie.

While waiting to be seated, I ordered an espresso martini, which definitely woke me up with a nice buzz throughout the meal.

Since it was already 2 pm, we ordered the Louie salad, Portobello fries, and a half and half Calabrese and Pepperoni pizza to share.

Louie salad was refreshing with pieces of blue crab and chunks of avocado. The Portobello fries were warm and chewy, and I can see why they're a favorite amongst diners. Nearly every table around us had ordered them! The pizza was made oven fired and thin crust, which is how pizza should always be made. We ordered half and half but if I were to come again, I'd order Calabrese instead because I like the spicy and sweet notes from the peppers and honey.

For dessert, we got a box of macarons, which were light but also decadent because of the filling. My faves are the salted caramel and the earl grey.

Pizza (yes), Calamari (yes), French Onion Soup (no) and the surcharge (no,no,no...)

First thing I look for in a return trip is consistency and BL did not disappoint, though I did have one blip "on the screen". First let me say the service was very good. She was attentive and seemed to read our minds at times when it came to ordering drinks. We had the Calamari (no photo) and it was probably the best I have had. The breading was light and airy. The calamari itself was fresh and tasty. Get this if you want a fabulous appetizer. Our Bianco pizza was cheese only (which we wanted) and it too was warm and tasty. The arugula gave it a nice freshness. Will order this Bianco pizza again next time we visit here. Now for the "kind of" bad news. The French Onion Soup was not good tonight. It was watery and had very little onion taste. This was an aberration from my previous visits. I think the chef missed some ingredients tonight when making this batch of French onion soup. Too bad :(
One more thing, the 5% surcharge is not a good business practice. One of those things that just feel dishonest. I love eating at BL's but this charge really turns me off. Bottega Louie's should just increase their dinner prices rather than add this secret surcharge. Overall a very good meal with a blip (or two). Enjoy!

Elite 26

4 photos
Believe the hype! This place definitely delivers on food, service, & ambience. As soon as I walked in, the tantalizing aroma made my tummy rumble for what was to come. I sat by the pizza making station which was fun to watch while waiting for the food.

Our waitress was very attentive, patient, personable, & offered great recommendations on food & wine.

10/10 - Tomato Bruschetta: the tomato was fresh, bread was the perfect crisp, & the balsamic with basil oil added even more freshness; I could eat this entire thing.

10/10 - Caesar Salad (anchovies on the side): this looked like a typical salad, but it delivered on all the flavors; every romaine lettuce was coated perfectly in dressing, the croutons had a great crunch, & having the anchovies on the side gave everyone the option to add it in themselves.

10/10 - Lasagna: another dish that's chef's kiss! The lasagna had so many layers filled meats & cheeses but wasn't too heavy; it had the right amount of sauce, so eat bite was perfect.

9/10 - Calamari Fritti: solid fried calamari with just enough breading & seasoned well; can't go wrong with ordering this if you like calamari.

9/10 - Calabrese Pizza: this is like an adult version of pepperoni pizza; the chilis were spicy, but it paired splendidly with the salami & honey; overall great choice.

7/10 - Napoli Pizza: the flavors were okay, but nothing spectacular; the tomato sauce was bright & the toppings weren't too heavy.

7/10 - Chèvre Al Limon: this appetizer divided the group, some liked it while others didn't; it's a unique offering of goat cheese plated with lemon, honey, & toasted pine nuts; for me tasted this a bit like lemon soap, but if you like goat cheese & something unique, give this a try.

Located in the heart of LA on Grand Ave, Bottega Louie charmed my taste buds and sweetened my day. Walking into the restaurant, described as a Gourmet Market, Patisserie, and Cafe, is like walking into a flower field. They have their beautiful desserts from macaroons to cake slices, and their pastries lined up to display. Each item on the display is a work of art. Restaurant and bar seating is on the left side. This layout makes it perfect for a casual coffee meet-up to a fun celebratory lunch or dinner.

My boyfriend took me here for a nice brunch while we were in the area. We arrived around 10:30 am so we got their brunch menu. We ordered the Mache Salad, Eggs Benedict, and Portobello Fries to share. The absolute show stopper to me was the Portobello Fries, which was the reason my boyfriend wanted to take me here as a crazy "fungi fan" or "mushroom enthusiast." Imagine the earthy taste of Portobello Mushrooms battered & fried, tossed with salty Parmesan cheese and herbs, and dipped with aioli sauce. To me, it was my version of mushroom paradise. It's decided - I can't go back to regular fries now that I know these Portobello Fries exist. Seriously, it's a must-try!

I think we ordered the perfect amount, not to mention, with the help of our amazing server. The Mache Salad was light and refreshing with the snap peas, celery, avocado, chicken, and lemon vinaigrette dressing. The Eggs Benedict was also made well - I'm talking the perfect toast on the English muffin, great hollandaise sauce, and a thick cut of Canadian bacon. Sharing three dishes was the perfect brunch meal that left my boyfriend and I full, but not "too full" if you know what I mean that we couldn't walk back to the car. Haha!

Definitely stop by Bottega Louie for a amazing time with great food and wonderful service.

STRAWBERRY ROSE
Iced drink that tastes vaguely of strawberries and rose. It's not made of real strawberries or rose and had that fake flavor, but still it was refreshing on a hot day. It also had a sour taste that made me think they should have called it a lemonade.

ÉCLAIR CELEBRATION
Tasted like a strawberry éclair. But also had a tart taste. The pastry choux was on the dry and harder side, but I did briefly put the éclairs in the fridge, so it won't melt from all the heat. The éclair was disappointing nonetheless. There was nothing special about it.

ÉCLAIR VANILLA
This was okay. Did not get a good vanilla flavor. Same as the Celebration éclair, nothing special about it. Waste of money.

NAPOLEON
The ONLY thing that was good. One of my favorite desserts! The crispy, flaky puff pastry and the pastry cream was done well. Everything was delicious!

CAKE MATCHA YUZU
Very sharp, sour citrus flavor that overpowered the matcha. Could barely taste the matcha. Wasn't very good and the cream was overwhipped and thick. Other jams or jellys inside were hardened too. The cake wasn't soft, but on the harder side. There were passion fruit seeds inside, which means there's passion fruit in one of the layers. So not sure why they call it Yuzu Matcha when there's no yuzu in it.

I don't know what happened, but the pastry selection was sparse that day. When I saw pics on Yelp, it seemed the display case would be filled with a vast array of desserts and pastries. There weren't even any macarons either! None! I was utterly confused and asked the person helping me, "Is this everything?" and he said it was everything. He looked at me as though I was asking the wrong question because one-third of the display case was empty. All in all, a complete disappointment! With so many new places to experience in LA, there's no need to visit again. DON'T WASTE YOUR MONEY HERE!

CUSTOMER SERVICE
It was okay. People weren't smiling nor welcoming, just doing the bare minimum.

I have strictly come only for the pastries, so this review is only for that and not the food service (which I will hopefully try one day).

For the price of their pastries, I would say they are all a great deal. The croissants are HUGE and priced the same as other bakeries around LA which sell smaller and lower quality croissants ($5-6). Take the ham and cheese croissant home, pop in the microwave for 15 seconds and satisfy your savory pastry belly. The apple turnover is HUGE at $5.50. Gonna emphasize that you really get bang for your buck here. On weekends, there's usually a short wait at the pastry counter, but moves pretty fast.

Cakes and tarts are beautifully presented and I've tried almost all of them. They're decent. My opinion on them is that they tend to be on the sweet side. They're a bit pricey, but not exorbitant. If you want to buy one to bring to a house party or whatnot and impress, these are great. But personally, after having tried almost all their cakes, I've moved on to other cake shops.

Luke L.
Elite 26
All-Star
San Gabriel, CA
39 Italian Food reviews
Nov 12, 2023
10 photos
I waited for over a decade, but I finally had a chance to visit the #1 most reviewed restaurants and food businesses on Yelp in the United States (https://blog.yelp.com/community/the-top-50-most-reviewed-restaurants-and-eateries-on-yelp/). Bottega Louie is a restaurant / gourmet market / patisserie and café located in Downtown Los Angeles. The restaurant is one of the most photogenic and popular restaurant in Downtown Los Angeles. Bottega Louie has another location in West Hollywood.

[Parking]: $20 valet parking and expect to wait 10 minutes to retrieve car. The parking garage across the street (725 S Grand Ave) offers $12 daily max from Monday to Friday before 4 PM ($2.00 every 15 minutes) and $7 in evening after 4 PM. Flat rate $7 on Saturday and Sunday. If you are lucky enough then it is cheaper to park via street metered parking (free metered parking on Sunday). The adjacent Whole Foods parking lot offers free 90 minute parking with validation at Whole Food, but park at your own risk as (1) one time I validated my parking ticket to shop at Whole and Foods and I still ended up paying for my parking ticket and (2) the lot is for Whole Foods customers only.

[Reservation]: The restaurant / cafe eliminated no-reservations policy and customers are now able to book a reservation through Resy. I actually booked a same-day 12:15 PM reservation 75 minutes ahead of the scheduled time.

[Service]: Pretty standard service as expected from an upscale brunch spot like this. Please note that the restaurant automatically adds 5% surcharge to mitigate inflation & other operating costs (it is not a service charge, gratuity, or paid to employees).

[Menu]: Yelp highlighted brunch items include Smoked Salmon Benedict / Eggs Benedict, Portobello Mushroom, Burrata Pizza, and French Toast. Items like Trenne Pasta, Pork Chop, and Braised Prime Rib Eye are only available during dinner hours. Lastly don't forget to take a look at their colorful macarons near the front entrance.

***

Smoked Salmon Benedict (Poached eggs, smoked salmon, crème fraîche, red onions, sautéed spinach & hollandaise sauce on hash brown potato pancakes - $32): This dish was alright and all within expectations - hash brown didn't really enhanced the overall texture for poached eggs and smoked salmon.

Burrata (Mozzarella, burrata, prosciutto di Parma, pecorino romano, sauteed rapini, minced garlic & extra virgin olive oil - 14-inch pizza $36): Amazing cheese and this pizza is definitely a must-order. It was enough portion to share among 3 full sized adults.

This is a perfect restaurant to have a wonderful brunch or dinner with a date; however I am not a fan of 5% "inflation" surcharge as each item on the brunch menu is already pretty expensive. Delicious pizza, decent service, and average benedict. I can't fault anyone for visiting this foodie trap with the spectacular decor and eye-catching baked goods section.

See all photos from Luke L. for Bottega Louie

10 photos
Overall: 4.6/5 (dine in)

My friends and I came for coffee and pastries which had a different seating area from the restaurant. They had a great variety of pastries, desserts, and drinks for a reasonable price.

Zeppoli ($5): This is an Italian pastry consisting of a deep-fried dough topped with sugar. It's very flakey, and you get that crunch from the granular sugar. However, it was more on the bland side so I didn't care for it.

Pretzel Cheese ($4.50): This is very different from the pretzels I had at Auntie Anne's or Wetzel's Pretzels. You barely taste the cheese so I'm not sure what I was tasting. I didn't like it but this was my friend's favorite.

Monkey Bread ($5.50): This is an explosion of flavors because it has so many things in there - you get cinnamon, chocolate, & walnut all from one bite. I think it would have been better warm instead of room temperature but it was definitely one of my favorites. A very close first to the chocolate hazelnut supreme croissant.

Chocolate Hazelnut Supreme Croissant ($9): Had to get this since I've been seeing this all over TikTok, and this was my favorite pastry. I love the croissant taste and texture. It had condensed layers so it's not as flakey as the zeppoli but it tasted better. The chocolate hazelnut topping and filling wasn't too sweet but I think there was a bit too much of the chocolate filling. If we didn't split this between the 3 of us, I would say the chocolate would have been overwhelming and the monkey bread would have been my favorite.

16 Oz Iced Lavender Latte With Oat Milk ($6.25): Wow, this was really good. The barista gave me the latte with the layers all separated instead of mixed up. I barely saw a thin line of the lavender syrup so I thought the flavor would be light but I was wrong. The latte was well balanced and delicious!

This is THE place to be in the morning with a drink and pastry in hand... but I went at night because work obligations call first, unfortunately. Even though I went late in the day, they still had a variety of pastries left of which the raspberry beignet and monkey bread caught my eye.

Monkey bread is such a nostalgic childhood snack for me and this one was a much more eloquent version than the one my mom always made. It had a beautiful flaky outer crust with the most buttery, sweet cinnamon-y center. The pull-apart aspect is my favorite part of the pastry and with every pull, there was a mixture of pecans and chocolate chunks.

The raspberry beignet was like your typical doughnut with a sugary dusting and raspberry filling. There wasn't really a wow factor.

My drink of choice was the Matcha Nitro Latte which I'd never heard of before. The kind lady explained to me that it was ceremonial matcha concentrate with nitrogen-infused cold brew. The result was a really light, airy drink that I honestly could've drank in just 3 sips. We got one regular and one with lavender syrup which I highly recommend. The floral note adds a great depth of flavor to the fluffy matcha drink.

I had such a great experience here overall with both customer service and ambiance. I love natural light and the window seating was perfect. With a large, luxurious pastry selection and a unique drink menu, this is a great place to catch up with friends.

Fluffy raspberry beignet

Monkey bread with dark chocolate chunks and pecans

Andrew D.
Los Angeles, CA
50 Brunch reviews
May 14, 2024
2 photos
Yeah, the hype is real. As someone who came in with no expectations aside from the word-of-mouth from macaron aficionados on social media and friends, I was pleasantly surprised with how, well, excellent everything operates at Bottega Louie. From the flexibility with the waiting window for reservations (traffic and parking on any given night is a nightmare in DTLA), the fast service, to the quality of the food--Bottega Louie's team brings their A-game to the table.

What I tried:

Nitro Oat Milk Draft Latte: Nitro Cold Brew concentrate, oat milk, agave sweetener. Solid coffee beverage.

Lasagna: Best dish from the lot; meaty ragu, an array of Italian cheeses and cream sauces (Béchamel), layered between thin pasta. A hearty dish.

Burrata Pizza: Burrata, Mozzarella, Prosciutto, garlic, drizzled with olive oil.

Bianco Pizza: Mozzarella, ricotta, garlic, Parmigiano Reggiano, and arugula. I prefer the Burrata solely because the Bianco goes heavy-handed on the arugula; a delicious pizza if you don't mind an abundance of arugula that overpowers the other ingredients between bites.

And...what Bottega Louie is known for...macarons. Call me uncultured, uncouth, and downright unadventurous--I had never tried a macaron before my visit to Bottega Louie; I'm the "Go big or go home," type of guy when it comes to desserts, and macarons always seemed so petite and unsatisfying to me. Well, I actually enjoyed the chocolate macaron I purchased on my way out the door--small but hit the spot!

For all those of you that are adverse to dining at seemingly overhyped or overtly expensive restaurants, give Bottega Louie a go; you'll get both quantity and quality along with some ritzy pictures for your social media page!

The Lasagna. As good as it looks.

Half Bianco, Half Burrata.

Pranjali S.
Elite 26
San Diego, CA
95 Brunch reviews
May 14, 2023
10 photos
We were lucky to get seated immediately after showing up on a fairly busy Sat during the USC graduation and Mother's Day weekend. I couldn't make reservations online so I assume they didn't have a reservation system.

When you walk in, you get a full view of their bakery section, the delicious macarons and pasties on the right and the open view kitchen on the left. The whole place has a relaxed, modern and fancy-casual feel. It is definitely loud, thanks to the open layout. So you do have to scream into people's ears. The service was very nice but could've been a little more prompt.

We ordered plates to share so we all tasted a bit of everything - the lobster hash, the smoked salmon Benedict, the calamari fritti and the Louis salad. I got an iced matcha green tea latte which was very very good for a matcha lover.

The smoked salmon Benedict was the best of all the food. The salmon had a slight tarty-spicy kick to it which I enjoyed. The hash cake it lay on was also delicious. The hollandaise was well done as was the poached egg. All in all, great recipe.

The lobster hash sounded much better than it was. The hash was delicious. The lobster could've had a little more salt or spice to it as it was pretty bland. The sauce it came in was too liquid and had a yolky taste to it which I didn't particularly love. Some of the greens accompanying the dish were also little bitter for my taste buds. So, a dish that sounded tastier than it was.

The calamari was as expected. Nothing too fancy, nothing too out of the ordinary. It was a nice accompaniment as a smaller plate with 3 other big plates.

The Louis salad was delicious! As a rule, I don't order salads because I don't consider it a full meal. But this salad was a tasty medley of greens, crab, avocadoes and a dressing that got my taste buds singing. It was also a huge portion! Among the four of us, we had a hard time finishing everything.

As a dessert, we first ordered the almond pistachio cherry pastry which deserves an entire star in itself. It looked so so perfect and, if it is even possible, tasted better than it looked! The pistachio jaconde cake was moist and light, the cherry marmalade was perfectly sweet and firm and the almond and pistachio mousse was so so tasty. We cleaned that up!

We then also ordered a limonchello which was a tarty tart with a limonchello curd and limonchello cloud with pralines. Now, as a rule, I'm one of those tart-loving people who complain "not enough lemon, needs more lime..." Well, ladies and gentlemen, not this time! This was so so tarty and just the right level of sweet that I couldn't get enough of it! The tart itself was a little firm and we were so full, I only licked off all the limoncello curd and the cloud. I'm not a fan of pralines, especially when they interfere with my soul-calming experience with limonchello or lemon or lime tartness. So maybe they should get rid of the pralines.

All in all, the food is good but those pastries blew out minds. Come here for the pastries. I wish I could've tried the macarons but we were so full that we could not. So next time it is!

See all photos from Pranjali S. for Bottega Louie

Iris L.
Elite 26
Alhambra, CA
21 Brunch reviews
Jul 4, 2023
9 photos
I have been wanting to check this place out for a while, and finally made time for it recently. The place is pretty spacious, not a lot of decor in the dining room.

Originally, I thought it's a chic place for a quiet brunch, it turns out to be the opposite. There's no music played in the dining area. All I heard about were people talking around me. I happened to be sitting on the bench area and I felt every step when the little kid was jumping next to me. While I was waiting for my server, I had nothing to do but to look at other people which were sitting on the other side of the room, which was awkward. The tables were a bit closer than what I would've liked. As far as the food goes, I ordered the pancake, lobster hash and portebello fries.

Lobster hash- comes with 2 poached eggs with lobster on top, surrounded by a sauce similar to lobster bisque sand hash at the bottom. The lobster is not overcooked or rubbery, which is nice.

Le pancake- it's a nice souffle pancake with strawberry at the bottom, with strawberry sauce on the side. I like the fluffy texture and small amount of crispiness on the edges. I would definitely get it again if I ever come back.

Montebello fries- it's portebello mushroom with a batter and you dip it in the garlic aioli. I am uncertain what the hype is about for the fries. The batter for the fries is pretty thick, almost reminds me of potato wedges. It's good but not that great.

One thing that I didn't like was the fact that they added a 5% surcharge due to inflation. The restaurant could've just printed new menus and reflected the cost rather than add an additional charge at the end of the tap. Then on top of that, customers still have to tip. My brunch for 2 turned out to be a bit over $100, which is on the pricer side for brunch.

I also ordered an apple turnover and 2 macaroons to go. The apple turnover was pretty sweet, sweeter than my liking. I ordered the earl grey and coffee macaroon. I don't really like the earl grey since it has chocolate in the middle. The coffee one is pretty good

Gretchen K.
Elite 26
Kissimmee, FL
47 Brunch reviews
Feb 20, 2023
2 photos
This location has been on a shared bucket list with a good friend of mine, as it is the flagship store and many celebrities have been seen dining here. (Prior to the pandemic, my friend recalled a fan or photographer catching BLACKPINK's Jennie and Red Velvet's Irene enjoying a meal here and playfully fighting over the bill.)

After a fun morning at Melrose Trading Post, my friend and I, plus my dad, came here for brunch. My friend arrived before we did and put our name in. (The wait was 5 minutes max before we were seated.) Please note if you come before 3 PM on the weekends, the brunch menu is served through to 3 PM and they cannot accommodate their regular menu. (They have some of their staples like a few pasta dishes and pizzas, but you won't find the full offering on the brunch menu.)

There are two choices for parking - either you can do valet for the restaurant which is a flat fee of $30 or you can find a lot or garage near the restaurant and park and walk. Both my friend and I did the latter and found a structure across the street that charged $7 flat fee for the day. The walk to the restaurant was very short - go up to one of the crosswalks and cross, then go up to the restaurant on the corner.

Staff were polite and very on top of service - they would notice empty plates or when you were finished with something and would clear it for space on your table.

My friend ordered the carbonara, I ordered a pizza, and my dad got an eggs Benedict. We shared the beignets at the table.

The beignets were dusted in sugar and came with a tart raspberry sauce to dip/drizzle on top. The flavors balanced out nicely and kept the beignet from skewing too sweet or heavy.

Food came out a couple of minutes after we finished the beignets. They make the pizzas fresh in one of the hot ovens and we were sitting near one of the areas where they were making them. (It was fun watching our food from start to finish.)

Their sauce is good and they were generous with the toppings. The crust has a good crunch but I will admit with the sauce and thin crust that it could have the potential to become soggy at times if you didn't eat it right away.

My friend enjoyed her carbonara and my dad liked the Benedict.

I will admit this location is very different aesthetically from the one in West Hollywood. This one has more of an upscale, classic architecture with visible kitchen spaces and often it becomes quite noisy in there with everyone talking at once. Tables are put together a bit closer than the West Hollywood one so I would say this one feels more close in terms of how they packed parties in and maybe at times a little crowded. In contrast, West Hollywood was more relaxed but still had a balance of elegance and contemporary elements in the space. (Also it can be a bit of a tourist destination for people who hear about the restaurant or saw their favorite celebrities dine here once.)

I noticed the flagship didn't have as many flavors of their macarons out as they did at West Hollywood. It seems like this one was focusing more on the cakes and pastries.

Prices are mid to high - I would say this is a fun experience to do once in a while, but unless you have the means to do it more often, it can be a little pricey.

Pepperoni Pizza

Earl Grey tea and Beignets

THE BEST DESSERT, THE WORST PARKING, 5% CHARGE ON TOP OF BILL, BEAUTIFUL DECOR!

Oh lord, I have been wanting to try this place for quite sometime, and i am so glad I did!

Customer service: 10/10
For being a more upscale type of place, the people are so nice. To the woman who was seating people, to the bar tenders, and the cooks, Everyone was so kind. I appreciate that more than ever!

Food: 20/10
FRUIT TART--After dinner, (at Wokano) we stopped here to get my dessert (what is date night without a dessert, right?!) and I ordered quickly because the bartender said they were sold out of just about everything. He said he only had one fruit tart left and I took that so fast! Y'all....it was the best fruit tart I've ever had! Think of real Europe cheesecake, meets fresh picked fruit, meets fresh apple pie crust, meets a chef who said I'm going to get it right or else! Man, did he ever. It was not overly sweet, crunchy perfect fruit, and the texture was light and fluffy...just amazing. I cannot wait to go back and get another.

Price: 6/10
I love good food, but dang. I think $16.10 was a bit much for a small dessert. Like, Costco would give me a whole cake (lol)
The price is $14.00 then tax, then a 5% add on fee for workers. I wish restaurants paid their workers fair prices without having to charge us for it. The money they must make here is absolutely insane, so I pray they use it to pay their workers vs upping our fees. But that may be a different conversation for a different day.

All around: 8.5/10
The parking is hell on earth, the prices are a bit high, and the dessert does not miss. . I can cannot lie, I just might be back sooner than I think! If you can get past the traffic, parking, and prices, you'll just love it here too!!! :)

I'm really disappointed to write this review because I use to love Bottega Louie, but after moving out of the area for a few years and coming back for the first time last night I had a bad experience. We came in around 10pm to get drinks at the bar. First thing we noticed was bags of trash behind the bar, like someone was cleaning up but didn't finish taking the trash out. And we noticed it because there was a bad stench of trash.
Secondly, the staff was not welcoming or friendly at all. They were being short and snide with everyone like we just walked in right at closing. It took awhile for the bartender to acknowledge us even though the bar wasn't very crowded. Another patron noticed the state of disarray behind the bar and sensed the bartender's attitude. Thinking they may have been about to close the patron politely asked what time they close and the bartender said they closed at 12 am. Closing wasn't for another 2 hours! Yet the bar was left messy and the bartender was giving haughty attitude to everyone like we were hindering their closing operations.
Also, the drinks were 20 dollars BEFORE tax and tip. On top of that they added on some surcharge that was not a tip or tax, just a surcharge they added on top and they expected you to still tip and pay tax. We wanted to ask about the surcharge but the bartender had disappeared for a really long time after running our credit card so we eventually just signed the check and left.
I had a pear martini which was actually pretty good so I guess that's one good thing, but for that much I expect at least some decent service and a bar that doesn't smell like trash, this isn't a dive bar.
I'm hoping their macarons are still as good as they use to be, but as for the bar at night you're better off elsewhere.

Super cute Pâtisserie and restaurant. Everything was so aesthetically pleasing and I was surprised to see the flower arrangements we saw everywhere including the bathroom was real!

We came for lunch and had the carbonara, Trenne Pasta, tartufo (truffle) pizza, and the sea bass. Everything was delicious. The carbonara was one of the best I've had and the trenne pasta was fried and had a very interesting crisp and chewiness to it. The tartufo pizza was very interesting and is yummy if you're a truffle fan. Otherwise I can see it coming off as having a very strong truffle taste which could be difficult to eat for some. Our pizza actually was forgotten in the kitchen when it was made and so a new pizza was made and came out a little late (maybe 15 mins) and to our surprise it got taken off the check as an apology. The service here is so great and staff was so friendly and helpful.

In the front of the restaurant is the bakery with very beautifully made pastries, cakes, and sweets. We got some to go & they were put in a gorgeous pastry box and bagged for us. I enjoyed the experience and would definitely come again!

The cool thing about LA is that you can walk into a place like this in your PJs and no one will bat an eyelash because for all they know, you're a billionaire tech guru or a rapper. But let's face it, you are neither of these, nor do you belong wearing PJs to a restaurant like this. But hey, who am I to judge you, especially because I'm not a rapper or a tech guru and I went very underdressed.

The waitstaff is attractive and the host staff are very polite. They have over 200 seats so there are no reservations. Your entire party has to be there and then they will seat you or if there is a wait, put your names on the list.

The cocktail choices are very inventive. I went for the mule and wasn't disappointed.

Our server was a complete angel and despite having numerous tables, was able to keep up with us and we never once felt like we were waiting or that she was a ghost.

The food is spectacular considering I haven't doing GREAT Italian in LA. The bolognese and the pomodoro are solid.

The desert choices are endless. That's the first thing you'll notice because they have a huge display in the front.

Overall I'd definitely go back. If you dont like the food, there's all kinds of rappers and tech billionaires there so you'll definitely enjoy the people watching.

The most incredible place I almost didn't experience! I was visiting DTLA for an event at Crypto Arena. The weather turned bad and I searched the map to see what local food options were available. Stumbled upon this magical place that would've fit in well on SATC during its heyday.

I loved that food was prepared out in the open. I had a view of the pizza station with the beautiful brick oven and the fire in the back. A very elegant touch that kept me thinking of how great a date spot this place is.

I really enjoyed my brunch here. It was super close to our hotel and looked so bright and lovely though it's surroundings were dtla. Maybe I am getting soft from living in paradise though. Anyhow we walk into this huge bright airy space with a bakery in the front. The macarons and cakes were gorgeous colors, almost like jewels in a case.

They do take reservations which my cousin had wisely made in advance. The noise level was high bc of the space so it was a little hard to hear conversation. The bathrooms were really clean and nice and they have the fancy thick paper towels to dry your hands!

The food was really nice - my fave was the portobello fries. I guess I didn't know what to expect but these were gigantic sticks covered in a thin crunchy batter as big as a zucchini stick! The sauce they give you is some kind of aioli which was a perfect accompaniment. Also got the arugula fennel salad which was refreshing and not overdressed. The burrata pizza also yummy and I'm still enjoying the leftovers. The broccoli rabe is seasoned with a little red pepper.

The best dessert was the napoleon - the cream is delicious and not overly sweet and the pastry is flaky and crunchy. The chocolate eclair was fine. More beautiful and delicious. How do they get the glaze so shiny and smooth?

Our server Kerry was super friendly, competent, attentive. Overall a great experience. 5% kitchen fee or whatever people are calling it lately so don't be surprised. It's not part of the gratuity.
